href="/wiki/Michael_Hill_(baseball)" title="Michael Hill (baseball)">Michael Hill</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Miami Marlins</b> are an American <a href="/wiki/Professional_baseball" title="Professional baseball">professional baseball</a> organization based in <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a>, <a href="/wiki/Florida" title="Florida">Florida</a>. They compete in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> (MLB) as a member club of the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) <a href="/wiki/National_League_East" title="National League East">East</a> division. Their home park is <a href="/wiki/Marlins_Park" title="Marlins Park">Marlins Park</a>. Though one of only two MLB franchises to have never won a division title (the other is the <a href="/wiki/Colorado_Rockies" title="Colorado Rockies">Colorado Rockies</a>), the Marlins have won two <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> championships as a <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_wild_card" title="Major League Baseball wild card">wild card</a> team. \n</p><p>The team began play as an <a href="/wiki/1993_Major_League_Baseball_expansion" title="1993 Major League Baseball expansion">expansion team</a> in the 1993 season as the <b>Florida Marlins</b> and played home games from their inaugural season to the 2012 season at <a href="/wiki/Joe_Robbie_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Joe Robbie Stadium">Joe Robbie Stadium</a>, which they shared with the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Dolphins" title="Miami Dolphins">Miami Dolphins</a> of the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a> (NFL). The stadium was later called Pro Player Park, Pro Player Stadium, Dolphin Stadium, Dolphins Stadium, Land Shark Stadium, and Sun Life Stadium during their tenancy. Since the <a href="/wiki/2012_Miami_Marlins_season" title="2012 Miami Marlins season">2012 season</a>, they have played at <a href="/wiki/Marlins_Park" title="Marlins Park">Marlins Park</a> in <a href="/wiki/Greater_Downtown_Miami" title="Greater Downtown Miami">downtown Miami</a>, on the site of the former <a href="/wiki/Miami_Orange_Bowl" title="Miami Orange Bowl">Orange Bowl</a> in Miami. The new park, unlike Sun Life Stadium (which was criticized in its baseball configuration for poor sight lines in some locations), was designed foremost as a baseball park. The new park\'s name is a temporary one until <a href="/wiki/Naming_rights" title="Naming rights">naming rights</a> are purchased.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> Per an agreement with the city and <a href="/wiki/Miami-Dade_County,_Florida" title="Miami-Dade County, Florida">Miami-Dade County</a> (which owns the park), the Marlins officially changed their name to the "Miami Marlins" on November 11, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> They also adopted a new logo, color scheme, and uniforms.<sup id="cite_ref-MarlinsSplash_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-MarlinsSplash-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-NewMarlinsLogo2011_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NewMarlinsLogo2011-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Marlins have the distinction of winning a <a href="/wiki/World_Series" title="World Series">World Series</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_World_Series_champions" title="List of World Series champions">championship</a> in both seasons they qualified for the <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball_postseason" title="Major League Baseball postseason">postseason</a>, doing so in 1997 and 2003\xe2\x80\x94both times as the National League <a href="/wiki/Wild_card_(sports)" title="Wild card (sports)">wild card</a> team. They defeated the <a href="/wiki/American_League" title="American League">American League</a> (AL) champion <a href="/wiki/Cleveland_Indians" title="Cleveland Indians">Cleveland Indians</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1997_World_Series" title="1997 World Series">1997 World Series</a>, which was notable for <a href="/wiki/Shortstop" title="Shortstop">shortstop</a> <a href="/wiki/%C3%89dgar_Renter%C3%ADa" title="\xc3\x89dgar Renter\xc3\xada">\xc3\x89dgar Renter\xc3\xada</a> <a href="/wiki/Run_batted_in" title="Run batted in">driving in</a> <a href="/wiki/Second_base" class="mw-redirect" title="Second base">second baseman</a> <a href="/wiki/Craig_Counsell" title="Craig Counsell">Craig Counsell</a> for the series-clinching run in the 11th inning of the seventh and deciding game. The <a href="/wiki/2003_Florida_Marlins_season" title="2003 Florida Marlins season">2003 season</a> was notable for the firing of <a href="/wiki/Baseball_manager" class="mw-redirect" title="Baseball manager">manager</a> <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Torborg" title="Jeff Torborg">Jeff Torborg</a> after 38 games. The Marlins were in last place in the NL East with a 16\xe2\x80\x9322 record at the time. Torborg\'s successor, 72-year-old <a href="/wiki/Jack_McKeon" title="Jack McKeon">Jack McKeon</a>, led them to the NL wild card berth in the postseason; they defeated the <a href="/wiki/New_York_Yankees" title="New York Yankees">New York Yankees</a> four games to two in the <a href="/wiki/2003_World_Series" title="2003 World Series">2003 World Series</a>.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" style="display:none" /><div class="toctitle" lang="en" dir="ltr"><h2>Contents</h2><span links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Franchise_history">Franchise history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_Marlins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Franchise history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Miami_Marlins" title="History of the Miami Marlins">History of the Miami Marlins</a></div>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox mbox-small-left ambox-content" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><a href="/wiki/File:Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg" class="image"><img alt="[icon]" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/20px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png" width="20" height="14" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/30px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1c/Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg/40px-Wiki_letter_w_cropped.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="44" data-file-height="31" /></a></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs expansion</b>. <small>You can help by <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Miami_Marlins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=">adding to it</a>.</small>  <small><i>(August 2017)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Wayne_Huizenga" title="Wayne Huizenga">Wayne Huizenga</a>, CEO of <a href="/wiki/Blockbuster_LLC" title="Blockbuster LLC">Blockbuster Entertainment Corporation</a>, was awarded an expansion franchise in the <a href="/wiki/National_League" title="National League">National League</a> (NL) for a $95&#160;million expansion fee and the team began operations in <a href="/wiki/1993_Florida_Marlins_season" title="1993 Florida Marlins season">1993</a> as the <b>Florida Marlins</b>.\n</p><p>The Marlins would qualify for the postseason and win the World Series in both <a href="/wiki/1997_Florida_Marlins_season" title="1997 Florida Marlins season">1997</a> and <a href="/wiki/2003_Florida_Marlins_season" title="2003 Florida Marlins season">2003</a>, though both titles were followed by controversial periods where the team sold off all the high-priced players and rebuilt.\n</p><p>The Marlins moved into their new ballpark, <a href="/wiki/Marlins_Park" title="Marlins Park">Marlins Park</a> in 2012, which coincided with a change in the team colors/uniforms and name to the <b>Miami Marlins</b>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Series_championships">World Series championships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a text-align:center; width:100px; border:#aaa 1px solid;"><tbody><tr><td style="background:transparent;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marlins42.png" class="image"><img alt="42" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Marlins42.png/100px-Marlins42.png" width="100" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Marlins42.png/150px-Marlins42.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d3/Marlins42.png/200px-Marlins42.png 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="600" /></a></td></tr><tr><td><a href="/wiki/Jackie_Robinson" title="Jackie Robinson">Jackie<br />Robinson</a><br />All MLB<br /><span style="font-size:80%; white-space:normal">Honored <span style="white-space:nowrap">April 15, 1997</span></span></td></tr></tbody></table>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<dl><dd><i>See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_retired_numbers#Alternative_methods_of_recognition" title="List of Major League Baseball retired numbers">List of Major League Baseball retired numbers \xc2\xa7&#160;Alternative methods of recognition</a>.</i></dd></dl>\n<p>From 1993 until 2011, the Marlins had retired the number 5 in honor of <a href="/wiki/Carl_Barger" title="Carl Barger">Carl Barger</a>, the first president of the Florida Marlins, who had passed away prior to the team\'s inaugural season. Barger\'s favorite player was <a href="/wiki/Joe_DiMaggio" title="Joe DiMaggio">Joe DiMaggio</a>, thus the selection of number 5. With the move to the new ballpark, the team opted to honor Barger with a plaque. <a href="/wiki/Logan_Morrison" title="Logan Morrison">Logan Morrison</a>, a Kansas City native and fan of <a href="/wiki/Kansas_City_Royals" title="Kansas City Royals">Royals</a> Hall-of-Famer <a href="/wiki/George_Brett" title="George Brett">George Brett</a> (who wore that number with the Royals), became the first Marlins player to wear the number.<sup id="cite_ref-morrison5_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-morrison5-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>After <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Fern%C3%A1ndez_(pitcher)" title="Jos\xc3\xa9 Fern\xc3\xa1ndez (pitcher)">Jos\xc3\xa9 Fern\xc3\xa1ndez</a>\'s death as a result of a boating accident on September 25, 2016, the Miami Marlins announced plans to build a memorial at <a href="/wiki/Marlins_Park" title="Marlins Park">Marlins Park</a> in his honor. However, Fern\xc3\xa1ndez\'s number 16 has yet to be officially retired.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" href="/wiki/Dominican_Republic" title="Dominican Republic">Dominican Republic</a>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Marlins_Park">Marlins Park</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_Marlins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Marlins Park">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Marlins_Park" title="Marlins Park">Marlins Park</a></div>\n<p>The Marlins began construction of a new, state-of-the-art stadium at the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Orange_Bowl" title="Miami Orange Bowl">Miami Orange Bowl</a> site on July 18, 2009. The now approved stadium was the subject of a protracted legal battle. A lawsuit by local automobile franchise mogul and former Philadelphia Eagles owner <a href="/wiki/Norman_Braman" title="Norman Braman">Norman Braman</a> contested the legality of the deal with Miami-Dade County and the City of Miami. However, Miami-Dade County Judge Beth Cohen dismissed all the charges in Braman\'s lawsuit.\n</p><p>The seating capacity for Marlins Park is 36,742, making it the third-smallest stadium (in capacity) in the MLB. Its first regular season game was April 4, 2012, against the St. Louis Cardinals, the ballpark became only the sixth MLB stadium to have a <a href="/wiki/Retractable_roof" title="Retractable roof">retractable roof</a>, joining <a href="/wiki/Rogers_Centre" title="Rogers Centre">Rogers Centre</a> in Toronto (1989), <a href="/wiki/Chase_Field" title="Chase Field">Chase Field</a> in Phoenix (1998), <a href="/wiki/Safeco_Field" title="Safeco Field">Safeco Field</a> in Seattle (1999), <a href="/wiki/Minute_Maid_Park" title="Minute Maid Park">Minute Maid Park</a> in Houston (2000), and <a href="/wiki/Miller_Park_(Milwaukee)" class="mw-redirect" title="Miller Park (Milwaukee)">Miller Park</a> in Milwaukee (2001).\n</p><p>As part of the new stadium agreement, the team renamed itself the <b>Miami Marlins</b> on November 11, 2011 along with the unveiling of new uniforms and team logo in time for the move to the new stadium in 2012.\n</p><p>Until a naming-rights deal is reached, the park will be known as <b>Marlins Park</b>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Radio_and_television">Radio and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_Marlins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Radio and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Miami_Marlins_broadcasters" title="List of Miami Marlins broadcasters">List of Miami Marlins broadcasters</a></div>\n<p>The Marlins\' <a href="/wiki/Flagship" title="Flagship">flagship</a> <a href="/wiki/Radio_station" title="Radio station">radio station</a> from their inception in 1993 through 2007 was <a href="/wiki/WQAM" title="WQAM">WQAM</a> 560&#160;AM. Although the Marlins had plans to leave WQAM after 2006, they ultimately remained with WQAM for the 2007 season. On October 11, 2007, it was announced that the Marlins had entered into a partnership with <a href="/wiki/WAXY_(AM)" title="WAXY (AM)">WAXY</a> 790&#160;AM to broadcast all games for the 2008 season. Longtime <a href="/wiki/Expo_67" title="Expo 67">Montreal Expo</a> and current Marlins play-by-play radio announcer <a href="/wiki/Dave_Van_Horne" title="Dave Van Horne">Dave Van Horne</a> won the Hall of Fame\'s <a href="/wiki/Ford_C._Frick_Award" title="Ford C. Frick Award">Ford C. Frick Award</a> for excellence in baseball broadcasting in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> He shares the play-by-play duties with <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Geffner" title="Glenn Geffner">Glenn Geffner</a>.\n</p><p>Games are also broadcast in Spanish on Radio Mambi 710&#160;AM. <a href="/wiki/Felo_Ram%C3%ADrez" title="Felo Ram\xc3\xadrez">Felo Ram\xc3\xadrez</a>, who calls play-by-play on that station along with <a href="/wiki/Luis_Quintana" title="Luis Quintana">Luis Quintana</a>, won the Ford C. Frick Award from the National Baseball Hall of Fame in 2005.\n</p><p>Marlins games are televised by <a href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Florida" title="Fox Sports Florida">Fox Sports Florida</a>. FS Florida\'s slogan in 2008 was "You Gotta Be Here." For the 2009 season the new slogan is "It\'s where you wanna be." There are no games available <a href="/wiki/Terrestrial_television" title="Terrestrial television">over-the-air</a>, with the exception of games broadcast on <a href="/wiki/Fox_Major_League_Baseball" title="Fox Major League Baseball">Fox Saturday Baseball</a>; the last "free TV" broadcast of a game was on <a href="/wiki/WPXM-TV" title="WPXM-TV">WPXM-TV</a> in 2005.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_Marlins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Marlins_Mermaids_2009.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Marlins_Mermaids_2009.jpg/220px-Marlins_Mermaids_2009.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Marlins_Mermaids_2009.jpg/330px-Marlins_Mermaids_2009.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Marlins_Mermaids_2009.jpg/440px-Marlins_Mermaids_2009.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="2592" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Marlins_Mermaids_2009.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marlins Mermaids on June 19, 2009</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1989, <i><a href="/wiki/Back_to_the_Future_Part_II" title="Back to the Future Part II">Back to the Future Part II</a></i> had a reference to the <a href="/wiki/2015_Chicago_Cubs_season" title="2015 Chicago Cubs season">Chicago Cubs</a> defeating a baseball team from <a href="/wiki/Miami" title="Miami">Miami</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2015_World_Series" title="2015 World Series">2015 World Series</a>, ending the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Major_League_Baseball_franchise_postseason_droughts#Longest_current_World_Series_championship_drought" title="List of Major League Baseball franchise postseason droughts">longest championship drought</a> in all four of the major <a href="/wiki/Major_professional_sports_leagues_in_the_United_States_and_Canada" title="Major professional sports leagues in the United States and Canada">North American professional sports leagues</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Marlins were the first team in <a href="/wiki/Major_League_Baseball" title="Major League Baseball">Major League Baseball</a> to have a dance/cheer team.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> Debuting in 2003, the <i>"Marlins Mermaids"</i> influenced other MLB teams to develop their own cheer/dance squads; this was inspired in part by similar squads from the NFL and NBA.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> In 2008, the Florida Marlins debuted <i>"The Marlins Manatees</i>", Major League Baseball\'s first all-male dance/energy squad, to star alongside the Mermaids.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2011)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> As of 2012, the Marlins have abandoned the "Mermaids" and "Manatees" for in-game entertainment instead using an "energy squad", a co-ed group of dancers.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 2016, the <i><a href="/wiki/Miami_New_Times" title="Miami New Times">Miami New Times</a></i> reported that the team was involved in contract dispute lawsuits with both season ticket holders and vendors.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Finishes">Finishes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_Marlins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Finishes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" P\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_attendance">Home attendance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Miami_Marlins&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Home attendance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Other than their first few years as a franchise in the 1990s, the Marlins have consistently ranked as one of lowest attendance teams in the league, coming in last place (30th) several of the past 20 years. Even when <a href="/wiki/Marlins_Park" title="Marlins Park">Marlins Park</a> was completed for the 2012 season, attendance was only average for the first year, dropping down to second to last by 2013.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:center">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="5" style="background-color:#000000;color:#FFFFFF;;"><b>Home Attendance at Hard Rock
